( роЗ) роЗ'рпЗро▒ , роП'? asked the Prime Minister and Minister of National Policies and Economic Affairs:

(a) Will he admit that-

(i) the traditional gem miners in the Ratnapura District, the leading district in the gem industry that provides a significant contribution to the national income, are losing that industry; and

(ii) the reason for this situation is that the traditional miner has fallen into the state of a labourer among the businessmen who are engaged in large-scale businesses within this industry?

(b) Will he inform this House-

(i) whether licences have been issued to use backhoes in large-scale mining industry;

(ii) if so, the names and addresses of licence holders;

(iii) whether he admits that using of backhoes for traditional mining causes an injustice to the traditional miners as well as severe environmental damages; and

(iv) the measures that can be taken to prevent this situation?

( роЗ) роЗ'рпЗро▒ , роП'? asked the Minister of Lands and Parliamentary Reforms: (a) Will he inform this House - (i) whether a programme called "Bim Saviya" is implemented with the objective of settling land issues; (ii) whether the above programme is implemented in all districts of Sri Lanka at present; and (iii) if not, the names of the districts in which the aforementioned "Bim Saviya" programme is implemented?

(b) Will he also inform this House - (i) whether a proposal to expedite the aforesaid "Bim Saviya" programme has been submitted by now; (ii) whether foreign aid is obtained to expedite the aforesaid programme; (iii) if so, whether the said aid is provided as foreign aid or a loan; (iv) the financial value of such aid; and (v) the total amount estimated for the "Bim Saviya" programme?

(c) If not, why?

On 29th of November, Sri Lanka was badly affected by a disastrous tropical storm which had caused at least 14 deaths so far and destroyed roofs of houses and power lines. Despite warnings being received from overseas at least three days ahead, the Government agencies ignored them only issuing an advisory to the fishing community. This not only affected the people, caused severe damage to property and the economy of the country, but it is likely to tarnish the reputation of the country in the tourism industry and commerce, leading to a decline in the relevant industries.

Bр╖Ар╖П р╢Жр╖Др╖Пр╢╗р╢║р╢з р╢ор╢╕ р╢ЬN р╢Ср╖Гр╖К. Oр╖Ар╖Щр╢╕р╖Д$ р╢╕$MLр╢╕р╖П р╢Ър╢ор╖П р╢Ър╢╗р╢╜р╖П р╢Ер╖Ар╖Г$ р╢Ър╢╗$р╢▒ р╢Хр╢▒р╖С. р╢пр╖Рр╢▒р╢з р╢СLр╢╕р╖П р╢▒р╖П┬Ъ 4Q р╢╕р╖Пр╢пT. [12.20 p.m.] р╢Ь& (р╖Ыр╖Ар╢пJ) р╢Ср╖Гр╖К. xр╖Ар╖Щр╢╕5р╖Д. р╢╕р╖Др╢нр╖П (рооро╛;рооро┐2 (рпИро╡родро┐роп роХро▓ро╛роиро┐родро┐) роЪро┐. роЪро┐ро╡рпЗрооро╛роХ ) (The Hon. (Dr.) S. Sivamohan) Thank you very much, Hon. Chairman, for giving me the opportunity to speak. I want to express my views on some estimates done by the World Health Organization. Sri Lanka's expenditure on health, both public and private, was around 3.2 per cent of the Gross Domestic Product - GDP - or US Dollars 89 per head in 2012. Life expectancy has raised from around 60 years in 1960 to 74 years in 2012 according to the World Bank statistics. In Sri Lanka, the mortality rate of children under 5 years has fallen from 9.8 deaths per 1,000 live births to 9.6 deaths per 1,000 live births in 2013. These are good health indicators.

I wish to thank the present Minister of Health, Nutrition and Indigenous Medicine, Hon. (Dr.) Rajitha Senaratne and at the same time, the former Minister of Health, President His Excellency Maithripala Sirisena, for the valuable efforts taken to improve the health sector in this country. The success of Sri LankaтАЩs health sector is largely due to its effective public delivery system, which provides both preventive and curative care at low cost. Government provides healthcare free for all citizens and accounts for almost all preventive care and most in-patient treatment. However, the public health sector has inadequate capacity, limited access to specialist treatment and inconsistent service standards.

р╢Ь& р╖Г┬Й8 р╖Щ @р╢╕р╢пр╖Пр╖Г р╢╕р╖Др╢нр╖П (рооро╛;рооро┐2 роЪроЬро┐ рокро┐рпЗро░роородро╛ро╕) (The Hon. Sajith Premadasa) Hon. Sajith Premadasa) Hon. Member, I want to clarify two issues. One issue is, if grama niladaris or any other government officials are involved in embezzling funds, then I think it is a serious matter and you should take that up with the relevant line Ministries and make necessary complaints. So that, that kind of activity is prevented.

The second issue is, as far as selecting the beneficiaries for housing is concerned, we do not decide who get the houses. The Ministry of Housing and Construction does not decide who the recipients are. It is decided by the relevant District and Divisional Housing Committees where the representatives of the people, like you, can get involved and make sure that those who are most needed will receive housing. So, it is up to you to participate at the District and Divisional Housing Committees and make your recommendations in order to accommodate the wishes of those who most need housing.

Thank you. р╢Ь& ┬Ыр╢н┬З р╖Щр╢║5р╖Щр╖Д@р╖Гр╖Кр╖Ар╢╗. р╢╕р╖Др╢нр╖П (рооро╛;рооро┐2 роЪрпАройро┐род)рокро┐ рпЗропро╛рпЗроХVро╡ро░ ) (The Hon. р╢Ь& (р╖Ыр╖Ар╢пJ) р╢╗р╖П┬Йр╢н р╖Щр╖Г@р╢▒р╖Пр╢╗8р╢▒ р╢╕р╖Др╢нр╖П (рооро╛;рооро┐2 (рпИро╡родро┐роп роХро▓ро╛роиро┐родро┐) ро░ро╛роЬро┐род рпЗроЪройро╛ро░рой) (The Hon. (Dr.) Rajitha Senaratne) Hon. Member, what we want is to implement your ideas. There are the Delft Island, other islands such as Nainativu, Mandaitivu and other places which are under the Northern Provincial Council. These are good proposals. What you propose is to send doctors from the Jaffna Hospital and other hospitals who are on punishment to those islands on rotation. If you can get that approved by the Provincial Council and send that to me as a proposal, then I will approve and get it implemented.

Faizal Cassim - Deputy Minister of Health, Nutrition and Indigenous Medicine) Bismillahir Rahmanir Raheem.

Hon. Chairman, I am very happy to speak on the Votes of the Ministry of Health, Nutrition and Indigenous Medicine and the Ministry of Housing and Construction.

First of all, I want to thank my Hon. Minister, who is dedicated, and the staff. I thank the Hon. Minister, for he never interferes with my work. He has given me freedom to work and develop the health sector in Sri Lanka.

I also wish to thank our former Secretary, Mr. Anura Jayawickrama, who gave us a helping hand in a big way in our work at the Ministry of Health, Nutrition and Indigenous Medicine, the present Secretary, Mr. Janaka Sugathadasa, the former Director-General of Health Services, Dr. Jayasundara Bandara, who left our services last week, the newly appointed Director-General of Health Services, Dr. Anil Jasinghe, a very experienced officer who has been with us, and I hope that he will carry on with his good work in the future too, the Deputy Directors-General, the Directors and all other officers. I have to thank them because they have been helpful to me in developing the health sector during the past few years.

I also have to thank the Hon. Minister of Housing and Construction, the Hon. Sajith Premadasa, for having given 20 to 50 houses for people in Pottuvil.
